	Too far down can't deliver promised room	The main reason to stay at the Embassy Suites is that it allegedly offers suites with two double beds, meaning a family with two teens can fit - you save the price of a second room. (Otherwise, this hotel being at the end of Manhattan, it's a 25 dollars taxi fare to mid-town).However, if that worked for us the first two times we stayed at Embassy Suites Manhattan, the past two stays our two-beds reservation turned into a King size bed and a cot - &quot;Or you can go somewhere else if you're not happy.&quot; Which we will do, the cot being freezing cold under the flimsy blanket, especially as it can only be placed next to the window. Even when you have a table, the hostess may try to remove your chair if you get up for more coffee, as happened to us - even though our daughter was still at the table. And if you protest, however mildly, you might invite a torrent of sarcasm, as my protest (&quot;Excuse me, my chair&quot;) did. So much for hospitality - what was her problem???? The business center: Two days in a row, we had to wait behind a bunch of kids who were working on .... I'm not sure what business they were working on. Lots of kids though, and you've got to wait. The suites need work - a lamp without a knob to turn it on, some mildew in the bathtub, a bent towel rack hidden by towels that fell into the toilet when you reached for them, the rack being bent.....So, if you can get your two beds out of the desk, it might be worth it. Bring lots of patience to the buffet and the business center. Otherwise, look mid-town. We will.

Nov 14 2009 	Definately Worth Staying...	This hotel was booked by the travel agent used by my office. This hotel lived up to that criteria and actually surpassed it. From the moment of arrival, the &quot;face&quot; of the hotel was friendly, efficient and professional. I am pretty picky about the cleanliness of hotels and how up-to-date the furnishings are although perfection is neither necessary or likely anywhere you travel. The room was very clean as was the bathroom. (Although I always travel with lysol wipes to clean countertops, phones, etc upon advice from someone I know who used to clean hotel rooms!). The work space/ &quot;living room&quot; was separate from the bedroom. The bedroom had a door which was nice. The bed was a bit too soft for me, but it was comfortable. The linens were clean (yes I checked thoroughly). The only drawbacks are that: (1) the walls between rooms seems a bit thin (I could clearly hear the guest in the next room coughing most of the night); and (2) the work/living area has a &quot;window&quot; which looks out onto the hallway. I kept the curtins closed. The staff accommodated my request for a late check-out without a blink of an eye. Check-out is 12 noon and I asked for 1:30 pm. Note that parking is only available via &quot;valet&quot; with NO in and out privileges. I was only going to take cabs anyway so that did not pose an issue for me, but it is something to note. I had not realized how close the hotel was to the WTC site. Sobering experience to view. Breakfast is included in the rate and while not outstanding, it was good enough and particularly convienent. There is a Whole Foods Market about 1 block away if you want to eat healthy! I would definately stay here again either on business or pleasure.

Aug 5 2009 	Enjoyable stay at Embassy Suites	Our stay at the Embassy Suites in July, 2009 was generally enjoyable. Check-in at 4:00 on a Saturday afternoon was quick and easy. We were given a room on the 14th floor facing the Hudson River. The suite was large by New York standards, furnishings were pretty standard for Embassy Suites and were in good condition. The room was clean. Unlike most Embassy Suites, there is no guest refrigerator, only the mini-bar one that charges you for an item if you move it from its electronic sensor. Soon after checking in housekeeping came by with 2 bottles of water (for being a Hilton HHONORS member). The suite was quiet and be bed comfortable. Air conditioning worked fine. The door between the bedroom and living room was opaque glass, not solid wood, so if you wanted to keep one room dark for sleeping while the other one was lit that could be a problem, but we didn't have that need so no problem for us.The exercise facilities were very nice. There is a large public gym in the building that guests can access through a back door with a combination lock (they give you the code when you check in). On Sunday morning the place was pretty much empty.We missed the evening reception, but did go down for breakfast. They do have signs warning that it gets busy after 9:30, and they were right. When I passed by on my way to the gym at around 9:00 the lines were still pretty short, but by 9:45 it was about a 10 minute wait on either the cooked to order line (the one I chose) or the hot buffet line. The food was pretty standard for Embassy Suites (so it was pretty good). There were a few annoying things though. While you could get an omlette on the cooked to order line, if you wanted potatoes, bacon, or sausage with it, you had to wait another 10 minutes in the hot buffet line (while your omlette got cold). They were not available from the person who cooked the omlette. For some items, like pancakes, there was no need to wait on line at all, but there was no way to know that when you arrived. All you could see were the 3 lines for cooked to order, hot buffet, and cold buffet (I think was the 3rd). This was also the first Embassy Suites I've been to that did not have trays. This may have actually cut down on spills, but meant that you had to find a table, put down what you could carry on the first trip, and make multiple trips back in to get other items. The staff was very good about cleaning off tables though, so although it was very busy, I was able to quickly find a table.

The location is also great for going to the Statue of Liberty and seeing the re-building of the twin towers area. The hotel itself is very new and very clean. Breakfast was fantastic, lots of selection and no queues if you are early - kids just loved the food. There is a mexican restaraunt in the hotel which has really great food and nice service and there is even a cinema in the same building which was brilliant one afternoon when the tired kids wanted to watch Ice Age 3 and rest their feet!!! There is a lovelly childrens park just across the street on the river and lots of places to eat all around in the financial world center. Really recommend staying here if you have a young family. Also took a quick look in the fitness room and it was huge - pity I don't work out!! We met up with friends who stayed in a very expensive hotel in mid town with a view over a building site!!! They paid more for two nights than we did for 5 nights and our view was fantastic. Go for this hotel and ask for a view of the Hudson.

Jun 19 2009 	Watch the Hudson!	Way down near the southern tip of Manhattan, near Battery Park - so not quite so accessible to Times Square, for example, as some other properties. But great for access to the World Financial Center (which is where I had a business meetings to attend, on every occasion that I have used this hotel), so very convenient if that's where you're going.Also close to the sobering sight of Ground Zero ... Staff uniformly friendly and helpful. (Where is the stereotypical abrasive New Yorker? Certainly not working at this hotel!) If you ask for directions to a NY landmark they will whip out a map, mark the route for you, write down the bus numbers or subway lines you need to take, and / or order a taxi.Rooms (suites, actually) on the river-facing side of the hotel have a great view of the Hudson, and of the New Jersey shore, and in some cases of Lady Liberty. Personally, I enjoyed it - watching the river traffic, the ferries; occasionally even a helicopter, flying by no higher than my room it seemed to me!Rooms / suites on the other side look out on buildings, I think - I only stayed one night in a room on that side, and then requested a change, which they very promptly obliged me with. Room rates are slightly higher on the side with the view ... :) All suites quite spacious, certainly by European standards.Outstanding Western-style breakfast - eggs any style, prepared in front of you, waffles, pancakes, sausages, rolls, bagels, the works.As some other reviews mention, this hotel is very much in a business district, so the streets around do get deserted after dark - which can be a little unnerving. The nearest subway stop is about a 10-minute walk; but there are always taxis available just outside the hotel.Not necessarily a great location for a tourist visiting NY for the first time, but absolutely perfect for business visits in the area.

Each evening we therefore had a great start!The hotel was close to Ground Zero and there is only about a 10 minute walk via raised walkways across the main West Side Highway to the nearest tube station. There was a constant supply of cabs outside the front door of the hotel if you preferred that method and the cost for 4 of us to mid-town (ie Times Sq) was about $14 - so not bad when split 2 ways. The daily unlimited tube card of $7.50 is good value if you are visiting several areas in a day and want to hop on and off the tubes. By accident we found restaurants and shops in the World Financial Centre across from the side of the hotel (opposite the window where the breakfast and manager's reception is). With regard to the Breakfast, although this is good value as it is included in the cost of the stay, we felt that it was not as good as the previous Embassy Suites we had stayed at. There was not as much choice - no cold meats, yoghurts or pastries and very limited cakes and fresh fruit. Also the 2 lines (one for the fried eggs etc and one for the bacon etc) became very congested and unless you were willing to push in to get your bacon, your eggs would get cold. I think this is something that the management should definitely look at and change. You are allowed to take bagels, cakes, bananas, milk, tea bags etc away for later in the day if you wish. However that is really the only complaint we had and overall we have given it a very high rating and would definitely recommend this hotel on all counts.

The money didn't bother us too much, but we did seem to spend a long time in the back of cabs.It doesn't have the unexpected &quot;holiday resort&quot; feeling of the Embassy Suites in DC; there's no swimming pool, and although you have access to a proper gym, it's a slightly intimidatingly professional one!The restaurant and bar is quite small, and is heaving for the &quot;free drinks hour&quot; late afternoon (for which you get a couple of drink tokens, unlike DC's unlimited drink arrangement). And if you go to breakfast after 8AM, it's chaotic, with potentially long waits for the omelette station.If that sounds a bit negative, I don't mean it to be. The hotel was clean, quiet and efficient, and offered us everything we'd want in a New York leisure stay with a young child. If the caveats above don't worry you, thoroughly recommended.(PS: there's a big multi-screen cinema within the building too, which was great)

One night we had 4 drinks each (G&amp;Ts). If you order the drinks at the last min you can take themt o your room. If you want to keep fit the hotel has a gym but we went running instead as the Battery Park is outside the hotel and you can run right down the Hudson wtih views of the Statue of LIberty. Mar 30 2009 	What a Bargain!	My family stayed at the Embassy Suites NYC the last weekend in March. We are two adults and one 5 yr old. The experience could not have been better. We arrived in NYC at about 11 AM, and were able to check in right away (regular check in is at 4). So that was a big plus. We weren't scheduled to leave until 2 PM, and the front desk gave us an extra hour to check out. That was another big plus. The doorman hailed a cab and loaded our bags in the cab when we left. The front desk staff were friendly and the bar and breakfast staff were helpful and friendly.The rooms are clean and modern. We paid for a regular King suite and ended up with a water view room, which was quiet. I can't comment on the noise level of the other rooms. The room is very big. It includes a bedroom with a door separating it from a living room. The living room has a comfortable fold out bed, which was outfitted with sheets when we checked in (big thumbs up for the housekeeping staff). Even one of those rooms alone was bigger than the entire hotel room of the last place I stayed in NY. There really isn't a fridge that you can use and don't even touch the little snacks on the minibar! If you pick them up for more than 20 seconds, you will get charged. (The front desk took that off the bill with no argument!)The full hot/cold breakfast was great, but maybe a little crowded. You could avoid the crowd if you got up early. I would have been happy with a bowl of cereal and cup of coffee, but got eggs, pancakes, bacon, omelet, etc. The evening reception was good and I appreciate being able to unwind after a long day of site-seeing and before going out. Don't expect make dinner out of it, as it is just a couple of free drinks and some chips. Others who commented here seemed to have a little more, so you might get lucky. We liked the location, though if you are looking to be in a real neighborhood and pretend like you are a New Yorker, or this is your only chance to visit NYC, you might not like it. If I had $400+ to spend on equivilent accomodations, I would probably stay in a different neighborhood. I felt good being in the Financial District with my little one. There is plenty going on on the weekend, so not a ghost town. There is also a river esplanade that is large and she could run around there without me worrying about traffic, etc. We also live close enough to NYC that I know I will be back again soon, and can try other hotels and locations if I feel like spending more money.We took cabs the entire weekend because 5 year-olds can't really walk all that far and are unpredictable in subways. But the subway seemed very close to me. A cab to the theater district cost between $15-$18 with a tip, so this was a good way to travel for us. If you want to go to the theater, there is a half price TKTS booth at the South Street Seaport, which was about a mile from the hotel. Not a bad walk.If you think you might like this place, then I recommend giving it a try!

Mar 19 2009 	Great Value Rooms View...but be prepared to walk or cab it!	Overall, I rate this hotel 4.5 stars. It is a great value, and I'm a repeat visitor. I stayed a handful of times over 2008 and once this January for both business and pleasure. You usually can get a rate under $200 and for what you are getting, it's a steal in Manhattan.Checkin: About 4-5 agents checking people in. Most of the time there isn't a line, but when there is it's usually quick. Depending on who you get, they are pretty accommodating or a tad too cool but always professional. Fresh apples in a bowl on the counter, so be sure to grab one or two. Elevators are quick and plentiful. make sure you don't go up the escalators because those take you to the dining area and conference rooms. Beautiful, contemporary, large building. Rooms: Huge! They usually honor my corner room requests, but I've stayed in the regular rooms and they are about the same size of some of my friends' studios. You have a bedroom that is separated by a door. Beds and linens are comfy, but it sucks if you and your significant other get stuck with a full-sized bed instead of a queen/king. Large television (pseudo flat screen), desk and ergonomic chair, free internet. I've always had a water view room, and it's pretty but the construction surrounding the building is not. Noice can sometimes be an issue, so bring earplugs if you are an extremely light sleeper. You will rarely hear hallway noise as you are separated and relatively far from your entrance door. There's a large living room that also has a television, table with chairs, couch, chaise, and leather coffee table. I hated this because it was weird balancing drinks and food on top of it. I was worried that it would easily tip over and spill all over their carpet, which for any hotel older than one month in this city is still amazingly clean and odorless. Refrigerator is useless, as it's filled up with their pay- for items. Plus, it's weighted so if you shift things around they may try to charge you for something you didn't drink. There's a small convenience store near checkin you can buy water, snacks, magazines and travel sized toiletries. Prices were okay, not cheap or ridiculously expensive. Showers are clean, towels are plentiful, and the amenities are Bath and Bodyworks. I usually ask for extra since I have long hair, and that usually comes within 15 minutes after calling for it. Food: They give you coupons for free breakfast and manager's reception. I've eaten their breakfast, which is really good for being complimentary. Pancakes, oatmeal, coffee, juices, hard boiled eggs, cereals, etc. I don't recall an omelette station. For the afternoon/early evening manager's reception, they offer free drinks, beer and some mixed drinks. I think we tipped the bartender but it's nothing to go crazy about, just a nice pre-dinner freebie. They also have a small selection of snacks, I think nachos and finger food type thingies. We had room service once, just desserts, and it took a little longer than expected. We expected something more tasty and though out, but it took me by surprise. For example, sundae is a bowl of cream, chocolate sauce, and an entire pint of Ben and Jerry's! Needless to say, after that we never ordered room service again. Too long and too much that has to be eaten right away as you can't store it in the room.Gym: This is a huge plus for us as we regularly work out. They let you use the NY Sports Club that is adjacent. You can walk there through a side door connected to the hotel. It's pretty nice considering most hotels use an actual bedroom and convert it by placing one treadmill and two yoga mats in there and slap a &quot;gym&quot; sign on the door. Anyway, it's like going to a &quot;real&quot; gym, so I liked that a lot. Location: Awful...as in the sense that you either walk a lot or take a cab. There's really no sensible subway station nearby. That is the reason why I hesitate a lot when I book here, but then the price and amenities balance it out and I end up booking here anyway. If you don't mind taking a cab everywhere, or walking rather far distances then this wouldn't bother you. But when I have to get to Midtown East it's a bummer. If you are going to spend a lot of time in Soho, it's about a $5-7 dollar cab ride away. The availability of cabs can get problematic when the hotel is busy. We had to walk about 5 blocks away to flag one down since we didn't want to wait in the long cab line.To sum it up, for a great value, and you want to be downtown, this is the place for you!	
Mar 18 2009 	Pleasantly surprised by the fascility and the service	I spent on night at the Embassy Suites hotel in downtown New York at the start of a business trip. I usually stay uptown but for the first time I had a client near this hotel. I was pleasantly surprised. The hotel itself is this giant structure built around an inner atrium. The guests leave the elevators and walk out to the rim of this atrium. and then walk along open hallways overlooking the floor of the atrium many many feet below. I've seen this arrangement before in other Embassy Suites and not liked it, because of the noise possibility, so I was very pleased to see that the room I was given was arranged with the &quot;living room&quot; on the inside and the &quot;bedroom&quot; away from the entry door facing the outside of the building.The hotel itself is on near the water and my room looked out over the river and a small park. People were walking and running in the park. There is a new building directly between most of the hotel and the water, so I am sure most rooms no longer have a water view. The hotel is behind the World Trade Center site and to get there from any ground based public transportation, you have to walk past the WTC site and an overpass that takes you over a highway. It's pretty convenient to the PATH train; the subway is a bit of a walk. There is a boat dock very close to the hotel that you can use to get to Jersey City.The room was nice. Two actual rooms in one suite. The larger room was a living room with a work table, couch, coffee table, dresser and television. There was also a microwave but no fridge (there was a mini-bar fridge but there was a sign not to use it for personal food). The bedroom also had a television, dresser and desk, as well as a closet unit, two bedside small tables, and a large window looking out over the street. Because of the building's location there was almost no traffic on the street at night and there was no street noise. The bed was comfortable and in general everything was clean and fresh. The bathroom was large and everything worked well. I used the internet: it worked, but was slow and often got hung up. This was true both over wireless and the wired connection. I used the gym: it's a New York Sports Club facility (you can enter with your key through a back door and just sign in) so it was very very good. Much better than most hotel gyms. The hotel offers a hot, cooked to order breakfast every morning as part of the room rate, and there are signs near the elevators subtly encouraging people to get there early. It's buffet style, not table service, and the hot items are cooked to order as you wait in a line. I got there at 6:35 AM and it was very nice. I got my eggs made the way I like them right away, but I imagine that later in the morning it would be total chaos! They also had some cold items (melon, yogurt, milk, cereal), coffee, bacon, sausage, fresh made pancakes. Room service was quick. The food was OK. It was not well described in the menu and was somewhat different from what I expected. The service was very nice though; in fact, service at the hotel was overall very good. The check-in staff for example were not familiar with the rate plan I booked the room under, and did the work to figure it out. The room service person was willing to correct the meal issue. The downside to the hotel is that it is isolated. You have to walk quite a distance and past construction sites to get to public transportation and at night this might be unnerving. There were no restaurants nearby that were open on Sunday night. Monday morning was very bustly, though. It did not feel like being in New York, which can be good or bad depending on your perspective. It worked for me for my purpose, but I might not want to stay there for a whole week, as it's not &quot;near the action&quot;.

The front desk was quick to greet us and check us in. They saw our reservation was for a King Room, but noticed we had 3 travellers and offered us the use of 2 Doubles instead. The view from our room was to the World Financial Center and Morgan Stanley (nothing too special). Our room (#514) wasnt too far from the elevators, which never took more than a minute or two to arrive. Housekeeping did a great job or cleaning and bringing us the extra towels and soaps requested quickly.The hotel was just right for our group, two teens and an adult. With 2 TVs and a door that shut between the living/bed rooms, we were able to have our own seperate space when we needed it. We saw many other families and young people at the hotel, but were never bothered by loud or obnoxious behavior. As far as the location of the hotel, we loved it. A typical cab ride into midtown ran about $15, and we walked most of the day. The proximity to World Financial Center and its shops &amp; resteraunts was nice. Also, there is a great view of the WTC site from inside the World Financial Center - across the street to the south.) The hotel has a Pizza Bolla (great pizza, a little slow when crowded) and an Applebees (average food, poor service) in the complex. Also, a movie theater on the first floor. Starbucks was across the street in the WFC, or a 10 minute walk at W. Broadway &amp; Chambers. The nearest subway was 5 minutes away via the pedestrian bridge at Vessey St. There was an Amish Market grocery just around the corner as well on W. Broadway for fresh fruits, the pear apple is a must have when in season!The Hotel staff also did an excellent job of making us feel welcome. Front Desk, Concierge, and Doorman always helpful. The Doorman informed us that a private car to LaGuardia was $40, and much nicer/more comfortable than a cab. Ask for these kind of tips from the staff, as it was a much better value than the $18/person shuttle offered by the site we booked our trip with.Overall, the Embassy Suites was a great place to stay, and will defiantely be where we go again.Extra Tip :: If you are staying in NYC for the first time, check into getting a limo service to drive you from the airport to hotel. We did this as a last minute whim decision, but it turned out to be one of the highlights of our trip. The driver was great and took us from LGA, down 5th avenue, thru Times Square, and to the hotel, all for $150. There are many companies that will do this airport transfer service, and it makes a great, lasting first impression of the city.

One thing to note is that taking a taxi from mid town or the theatre district back to the hotel can be difficult. We were turned down a few times by cab drivers to take us back to our hotel. Overall, we loved our stay at the hotel and plan to return during future visits.

Nov 17 2008 	High price - little charm	After having visited NYC many times, my wife and me recently stayed at this hotel for 5 nights after having read the reviews on this page - but must say we were left with disapointment. OK, the hotel is fairly new and clean, and the staff is indeed helpfull and doing their best - BUT, there is absolutely no soul or spirit to be found anywhere, and nothing to justify the high price other than big (double) rooms. Empty, sterile spaces with no charm, and very little to remind you that you're in one of the most facinating cities in the world. The rooms are big and fairly clean, but again nothing special. There are carpets (with accumulated dirt) in living- and bed rooms, which in our oppinion should be replaced with clean wooden floors - as is the trend in most good hotels these days (at least in Europe).The breakfast is supposed to be &quot;the best in NYC&quot; - which is very far from the thruth. Maybe we (being Norwegians) are spoiled here, but this did not meet our expectaions at all. It was rather a basic &quot;American style&quot; breakfast consisting of pancakes and jam / syrup in plastic jars, and large bowls of tasteless bacon and scramled eggs, and soft drinks/juice in plastic cups. Cheese, ham, vegetables, healthy cerials etc which should be expected at the &quot;best breakfast in NYC&quot; was nowhere to be found. And as for the rest of the hotel, the breakfast lounge is very, very boring and more like an ordinary work cantina.OK, the hotel did have a happy hour with free drinks every night, but this did not compensate for a rather dull impression of the hotel as such. Add that the hotel is far from almost everyting at Manhattan (apart from Ground Zero and it's close-by areas) and expencive, we can not see any reason for choosing this hotel for a NYC stay - at least not for a vacation. Better to choose one of the many good and stylish hotels in the Time Square area. At least that's what we will do next time we go to New York.

Oct 8 2008 	You get much more for your money at the Embassy Suites!	First of all, I was trying to find the best deal in Manhattan for Oct 3-Oct 7, and found that the Hilton/Embassy Suites website had better rates than all your travel search engines, like Expedia. Secondly, if you've ever stayed in NYC, having a suite for $249 per night, is an absolute steal! I believe you should book at least 3 months ahead to get good rates. What really topped the cake was the free morning buffet breakfast and the free nightly drinks and snacks. The nightly snacks were nachos with beef/beans/cheese-enough to call it a dinner. Upon arrival, I requested an upgraged room since we were Hilton Honors members (never hurts to try), and they gave us a room, 1028, with a beautiful view of the Hudson river (on the 10th floor!). If you stay here, try to get this view. The room was huge compared to most hotels in the city, and clean.It's nice to have a separate living area. And, who cares if the TV is not an LCD. It worked fine,when I got a chance to watch it. The website's picture of the outside of the hotel must be old, because there is a tall building of condos blocking most of the hotel's view to the hudson river. So, try to get the NW corner of the hotel with the Hudson river view. Just across the street, to the left of the hotel, begins a beautiful walkway to Battery Park, right along the Hudson river. The walkway is very safe and beautifully lit up, beautifully landscaped with trees and plants, and plenty of benches to relax. Some of the docked yachts were incredible to see. Next, for the people complaining about that it takes 15 minutes to walk to the subway, maybe NYC may not be for them, or they can pay $400+ to stay close to their sightseeing sights. Most people will be doing a lot of walking when visiting NYC, no matter where you stay. It took us 10 minutes to walk to the subway, and we enjoyed the scenery. If you're staying at this hotel and plan on going uptown every day, thie subway is the cheapest way to go. Just be sure you get on the right trains- uptown to Central Park and Times Square- downtown to World Trade Center and The Embassy Suites. We found the subways to be very safe and conveniently located all over Manhattan. Little Italy and China Town were great sites to see, and I believe you can even get a different subway train, if you don't want to walk it. Even the walk there was not so far, for us. Overall, I think this hotel was a bargain for the emenities provided. This hotel is a bargain for NYC, and I would recommend it to anyone.

The two-room standard suite was perfect for putting the baby down at her normal bedtime and allowing us to sit in the other room and watch tv without having to be ultra quiet.There is a lot of construction going on with rebuilding the WTC, but there are ped walkways over the west side highway and lots of signs to route you in the right direction. Multiple subway lines are close by (&lt;10 min walk), as well as various financial district attractions.The hotel is conveniently located to the walkways to Battery Park and directly across from the Irish Hunger Memorial and a great playground for kids (0-5+ yrs old). We walked all the way to the tip of Manhattan to see the Statue of Liberty one morning. The walk along the Hudson River path was beautiful, very well maintained and highly trafficked with walkers, joggers, bikes and strollers.The continental breakfast was fantastic. We did not have any issue with long lines b/c we're up early with the baby. There were so many options, I couldn't believe it. There was standard continental breakfast items like fresh fruit, cereals, breads/muffins, yogurt; but, then there was a hot food line where you could order bacon, eggs, sausage, pancakes, etc. You could also use paper/plastic to-go containers to take snacks away with you for later. That is practically unheard of these days in all you can eat cafeteria eateries. The bus boys were very nice and helpful with getting high chairs, etc for little kids. The free evening cocktail reception is in the same location, but the breakfast area is roped off and the bar is opened up. You get vouchers at check in for drinks and breakfast. We had at least 4 drink vouchers each for each night we were there. The hotel is very generous to say the least.I would definitely stay at the ESH NYC again and recommend to friends whether or not traveling with young kids (but the two-room concept if obviously great for kids).

There is a separate bedroom with 1 or 2 beds, and a living room with comfy chairs and a sleeper sofa. There is also a wet bar with a microwave and refrigerator. These rooms are actually larger than many Manhattan studio apartments.The breakfast is bountiful, and features made to order omelettes and other hot breakfast items, aswell as fresh fruit, yogurt and cereal. There is also an evening Manager's Reception, where complimentary alcoholic and non-alcoholic drinks are served, as well as snacks. This hotel is a great choice for those who want to get the most for their money while traveling to NYC. The location is excellent, although you must take a subway or cab to get to midtown; the subway is actually one of the highlights of the trip in my opinion. It is also quieter than the hustle and bustle you find in Midtown. You will not be disappointed when you stay here.

Fortunately the maintenance people were able to fix the problem while we were gone and we didn't have to change rooms. The next morning we awoke to the same LOUD pounding at the crack of dawn. We could hear our neighbors swearing at the noise as they left the room. We hadn't slept well so to be able to sleep we moved to the entry room with the hideabed and closed the bedroom door. We got some sleep but it was quite uncomfortable. At checkout I was a little surprised the staff didn't inquire about how our stay was. Did they anticipate our response wouldn't be positive? I politely asked to talk to the manager and let him know we didn't appreciate the constructions noise and we would have appreciated a warning in advance of booking. The manager played dumb about the noise initially, then when I specifically mentioned the loud pounding he informed us that everywhere in NYC it would be &quot;noisy&quot; and claimed they had no advance warning of the posts going in across the street. I really doubt this as the noise was so loud you'd think they would need a special permit. I suppose it's not thehotel's fault about the construction noise, but for all the pain and suffering we endured all the manager offered was to &quot;pass on&quot; our comments, which only left us more disappointed.

Two things I've learned through this process: Don't bring your own pillow to a hotel, and empty your suitcase outside of the house on returning from a hotel stay.

The Embassy Suites building houses a huge health club, an 11 screen movie theater, and a DSW shoe store. There are also numerous restaurants in and around the hotel. The bagel shop is especially good. A late afternoon reception and breakfast are included with the room. We did not make it to the reception but loved the breakfast. Two cooks make waffles and omelets fresh. The regular bar includes oatmeal, cereal, fruit, yogurt, danishes, bagels, breads, sausage, bacon, eggs, coffee, tea, hot chocolate, water, soft drinks, milk, and juices. It was a nice way to start the day. Go early. There is no line and plenty of tables.There is a lovely place to walk / run near the hotel. The Esplanade runs along the Hudson River. There are excellent views of the Statue of Liberty and Ellis Island. There were always people out and about. It appeared to be a safe area. There are security cameras and NYPD presence is evident. There is also a nice playground. It was filled with mommies / nannies and small children daily. There are lots of trees and flowers. The water taxis are accessed from this area.We loved returning to the Embassy Suites at night and getting away from the crowds and noise.

Jul 9 2007 	Mixed Feelings	A friend and I were visiting Manhattan to see my son who is living in NYU housing during a summer internship. We chose the Embassy Suites (which is located in the Financial District) because of the amenities and the fairly close proximity to NYU. The hotel offered a fair rate for Manhattan, a complimentary &quot;cook-to-order&quot; breakfast and complimentary cocktails and appetizers (the Manager's Reception) every evening. What a deal! (or so we thought) THE &quot;UP-SIDE&quot; - the hotel itself was great - modern and clean. The bellman informed us that the carpeting, furniture and bedding in our rooms was new. (Our suites were on the 5th floor.) THE &quot;DOWN-SIDES&quot; - there was always a long line for breakfast, the omelettes were the only &quot;cooked-to-order&quot; choice (everything else was buffet) and tables were not plentiful (we had to search). The line for cocktails in the evening was even worse and a place to sit was non-existent. In each situation, there was a definite feeling of being &quot;herded&quot; through. For such a nice hotel, this was very disappointing.  BUT MOST IMPORTANT - out of SIX taxi rides taken BACK TO THE HOTEL from other parts of Manhattan, only ONE cabbie knew how to get there (and that was our initial ride from the airport). Even when given the address and cross-streets, two cabbies TURNED OFF THE METER at $12.00 and admitted they were lost, one stopped and asked another cabbie for directions, and the other two were $17. fares once we finally arrived. The point being that even though you receive a free breakfast and cocktails( if you're willing to wait in line), you will spend a bundle getting in and out of the Financial District.  Of course, the bus and subway systems are less expensive transportation choices... but those are not very &quot;user-friendly&quot; for tourists and, in my opinion, the subway is not a good choice for night travel in this area. MY SUGGESTION - great hotel for business travelers with work to do in the Financial District, tourists need to stay further north on the island. FYI - I am an &quot;experienced&quot; NY tourist. I have visited Manhattan at least a dozen times in the past - for business and pleasure. Hope this helps.

We got some great pics of the hudson from our window. Breakfast was included and it was excellent. There were so many options to choose from. The queues were long on some days but that doesn't matter as they move fairly quickly. We also got drinks vouchers for the manager's reception each evening and there were snacks to munch on there too which was another added bonus. When the manager's reception is over around 7pm the bar closes, which is a pity as when you have a few drinks you just want to stay there! There is another bar though (Chevys).We were a little concerned that the Embassy Suites was too far away from the main busy areas such as Times Square, but in fact it was way better than staying in a very busy place. The subway is less than a 10 minute walk from the hotel and we got metrocards which were a great saver, highly recommend them! There are plenty of shops and restuarants near the Embassy Suites so you should check them out too (Century 21 in particular!). We went to Little Italy and totally agree with some previous postings that it is tacky and to be totally honest very dodgy! Also recommend taking a horse drawn carriage ride around central park, get to see all the main parts and doesn't take too long if you are short on time.Overall, we found this hotel to be brilliant and would highly recommend it to future vistors.	
May 21 2007 	Great Family Hotel in NYC	We are former New York City residents and actually lived in Battery Park City. We know and love this area of New York City.Battery Park City is located at the lower tip of Manhattan very close to the financial district but actually seperated from it by the West Side Highway. It is a residential area and sort of &quot;secluded&quot; in that it's location doesn't invite many people other than those who live in the area.Now, that can be a plus or a minus,depending on your perspective. For us, it's a big plus. If you are staying in BPC, you will most probably need to take a cab ride to your destination, although as with anywhere in NYC, you can opt for public transportation.This contrasts with the option of staying at say, a hotel located in Midtown, where you can literally walk out of your hotel to major sightseeing, shopping and dining.The tradeoff between the two is this sort of peaceful seclusion (again, as far as anyplace in NYC can be considered secluded) against a more convenient location albeit with a sort of hustle and bustle atmosphere. The Embassy Suites Hotel is an excellent choice if you think you would prefer this sort of &quot;peaceful&quot; choice, but don't mind being a bit away from the action. The hotel itself is very clean and the rooms are extremely large. We travel with our two boys and it is perfect for us. The sitting area has a couch that folds out and sleeps two. The hotel serves a buffet breakfast which is a really great spread and the boys look forward to it each stay. They also have a Mexican chain restaurant located in the hotel, but we have never eaten there. There is a movie theatre (very clean and modern) right outside the hotel.There are also several restaurants located very close by and also in the World FInancial Center (which is walking distance). The hotel is also across the street from the World Trade Center site. This is downtown Manhattan, and you can walk to the financial district as well as a myriad of small museums and places of interest. Although there are many great stores and places to shop, downtown is not THE place to shop in NYC. The one negative we have, and always have, is the poor job they do on valet parking. Anyone who has stayed here, used valet and is reading this review is now shaking their head saying &quot;Yep, I know exactly what they are talking about&quot;. It takes forever to get your car and we have been staying here for many years and they still can't get it right. Overall, we would highly recommend this hotel for any family visiting New York City. We think that the size of the rooms, the rates, and the great area offset any downside experienced by not being in Midtown.

Apr 22 2007 	Family of 4 Spoiled Rotten by ES!	Family of four stayed at Embassy Suites, NYC from April 14 - 20 in a King suite; boys slept on sleeper sofa in living room. This is a great hotel -- suite arrangement, free breakfast, free happy hour/drinks/snacks, free internet downstairs on the PCs in the lobby. Linens were clean and crisp; pillows &amp; towels were plentiful; decor was contemporary and tasteful; room was comfortable and fresh. Bathroom is large with nice amenities. Vanity table/mirror in bedroom made it easy for mom to dry her hair in the morning while someone else used the bathroom. Likewise, the &quot;bar&quot; sink in the little kitchen area was a great place for one kid to brush his teeth while the bathroom was in use. We had requested an empty refrigerator for our room because we knew we'd have some of our own food to put in it and we knew the mini-bar would be fully stocked with no empty room in it. We arrived the day before the &quot;storm of the season&quot; hit so it was nice to find a full-size umbrella in the room. We were on the 7th floor, directly -- and I mean DIRECTLY! -- across from the construction site, but this was fun! The noise didn't bother us, hotel must be well insulated. But it was interesting to wake in the morning and see the work happening on the 7th floor of the building across the street. Took lots of photos of the construction workers (they have nerves of steel!) -- they even posed for us. Then when we came back to the room at the end of the day we could see the progress made.Breakfast was OK -- very crowded on Sunday, but more manageable during the week. It would help if they provided cafeteria-style trays for carrying plates, silverware, coffee cups rather than having to make multiple trips to/from the table and food area. Same menu every morning: made-to-order omelets, pancakes (choc chip &amp; regular); scrambled eggs, bacon, sausage in warming trays; toast, English muffins, bagels, muffins, sweet rolls, cereal (though no granola or high-fiber selections), yogurt, melon slices, grapes, apples, bananas, juices (orange, cranberry, grapefruit), coffee, tea, milk, hot chocolate. One day the scrambled eggs in the warming tray didn't look too good, but the omelet cooks made some fresh for me. Can't beat the price, though:FREE. We figured we would have paid $50+ for four of us to have comporable breakfast every morning in a diner, so this alone makes Embassy Suites a great value.Free Happy Hour/Manager's Reception: drinks (drink coupons indicate beer &amp; wine, but it seems they had an entire selection of liquors and could make almost anything, including Manhattans, tequila sunrise, margarita, cosmopolitan), soft drinks &amp; juices, nachos, cheese squares, carrots, celery, tortilla chips, party snack mix, popcorn.Our room was quite far from the bank of elevators, so request a room close to elevators if you don't want to walk. Didn't notice noise from other guests; there were lots of families and lots of business travelers. Staff was pleasant and helpful; housekeepers greeted us with a smile and good morning when we passed in the hallway. This hotel is about a 10-minute walk to the subway stop; walked past the WTC site every day. Though we were concerned about being in a remote location at night, it wasn't bad at all. Across the street is the World Financial Center with shops, restaurants, drug store, and offices. There's a Chevy's restaurant accessible from the inside of the Embassy Suites, and a bagel place and a good pizza place as part of the same building of the Embassy Suites, but you have to go outside and around the corner to get to these. The area at large is an interesting mix of business and new residential. It is close to Tribeca, which seems to be an upscale neighborhood for professional people and young families. We saw lots of kids in strollers and even a group of older boys playing baseball in a neighborhood ballpark. There were several &quot;parks&quot; -- green areas with flowers, some for playing in and some just for looks. There were two children's playgrounds along the waterfront, which is also a pretty walk with nice paths. We felt safe and secure the entire time-- never felt threatened or worried about our safety. Lots of people walking around after dark.Embassy Suites doesn't disappoint. We were sad to leave -- we spent the last night of our vacation at another suite-brand hotel on Long Island to visit family. We were definitely spoiled by our time in the Embassy Suites; there was nothing at all wrong with our Long Island hotel, but because it followed our stay at ES, it paled in comparison. We'll stay at Embassy Suites again when we return to the city with our kids.

Apr 7 2007 	This hotel is still fantastic....	We stayed at the Embassy for five nights in March, having come over for St Paddy’s day and this was the second time we had stayed here, the previous being in 2005. The place hadn’t changed, it is still excellent. During our stay we had the added bonus of a foot of snow which made the whole area absolutory beautiful, and also demonstrated how roads and sidewalks can be managed during even the worst of storms. Within hours paths were clear and the Embassy staff had cleared the road outside. There have been a few changes since our last stay, mainly the construction of a large building right in front of the hotel. This is a shame as the view before can only be described as a panoramic beauty (see our last post for a photo), however if you request a river view room this is exactly what you get as the rooms in front of the Irish memorial still enjoy fantastic views over the Hudson. If you didn’t know what the view was before you would think this fabulous, which of course it is… The other change as others mention is that the breakfasts and managers reception is now done on a voucher basis, each guest has two drinks per night and a breakfast voucher per night of your stay. At first we were disappointed with this however you wont be in the hotel every night and to be honest we didn’t get through ours. Soft drinks and the snacks are all free and no vouchers are required.The hotel has an Applebee’s and a Chevy’s on site and we ate at both, Applebee’s is ok, nothing special – normal fare and thought a little pricey. I love Chevy’s the food is excellent and for the ladies the huge frozen margaritas are a must. This isn’t as good as the big one in Time Square but for convenience to your room it just cannot be matched.Also in the hotel there is a massive DSW (Designer Shoe Warehouse), this place is great. I managed to buy three pairs of Sketchers for about a fifth of the UK price, I lost track of how many pairs of shoes my wife bought…! For this place to in the same complex as the hotel (literally in house, just up an escalator from the hotel foyer) it just adds to benefits of staying here.There is also a bagel place on site, maybe they were having an off day but I bought a couple of wraps and they can only be described as disgusting, a shame really as this was the only bad food of the entire stay and they looked like they were going to be great.As far as getting to the Embassy we arrived at JFK and just took a cab - the fare is set at $45 plus toll and tip so it shouldn’t cost any more than $60 with a generous tip. We organised a return car through the concierge. This isn’t just a guy helping out his mate the hotel have an arrangement with a good company that provide a fixed rate service. Having had a horrendous experience getting to their airport last time this company was great and it only cost $70 all in.The concierge is extremely helpful as are all of the staff , if you have any questions just ask. There are six PC’s in the lobby and also a little shop which is priced very well, especially if you compare it to the minibar! Tip – there are vending machines for cans of soda etc on every floor.. $1.25 at the machines $2.50 from the minibar.There are several subway stations within an easy walk, I would say for most people it would take 10 minutes to reach them and the benefits of staying downtown is a great nights sleep away from the noise of the city.Be careful with the cabs, especially if you not from the USA, most are honest and OK but a fair few will try and take you on a roundabout tour of the city, if you go up Chambers street and then up 7th the fare should only cost around $11 to get you to Times Square – we had guys trying to take us up East river drive and trying to charge $20 plus. Also don’t expect the driver to know where you are going to, most have only been in New York as you have and unlike London cabbies they don’t have to pass the knowledge first. If you don’t know the location of where you want get to, ask the doorman or the concierge first.As you can probably tell, we love this hotel.. it is clean, friendly, the rooms are huge and modern, the beds are massive and comfortable, you get all the nice touches such as robes, toiletries and a free paper every day… We can’t wait to come back to this great hotel and to New York, the best city in the world.

We did not have any problems with construction noise. I really loved this area and the hotel was comfortable. I would definitely return. Feb 22 2007 	Great place to stay	We had a great stay at this hotel over 16th to 20th February 2007. Arriving at EWR we chose to travel by train to Newark Penn then take the PATH train ($1.50) to World Trade Center which was a 10 minute easy walk to the Hotel. A friendly arrival and check in, no bell boys dragging your cases away, 4 lifts to 15 floors, rarely had to wait more than 30 seconds. The room, well there were two rooms plus bathroom, were very comfortable, with coffee making, self-serve minibar which charged to your room as you took the item out and a cavernous safe. The view was fantastic, worth the extra for a harbor view, despite the new build block partially blocking the vista.A TV in each room, fair size bathroom but low and wide bath - more suited to the American physique? Hair dryer, two settees, a desk, big bed, and a number of restaurants on the premises. also a gym, free to use for hotel guests.Breakfast a little frantic at busy times, but plenty of choice, manager's reception a nice thought. Subway was around ten minutes away. A lovely walk along the waterfront down to the Circle Line ferries (30 minutes stroll) for Ellis Island and Statue of Liberty Brooklyn Bridge (50 minutes). Pick up point for Sight seeing buses around 15 mins away and buy ticket point around 30 mins away (next to ferries). Recommend red buses rather than blue ones, we and quite a few others had some difficulties with the 'sightseeing NY' company! Best buy was a 2 or 3 day ticket, hop on hop off plus Empire State visit (you jumped part of the queue) and a few others all included. Security at Empire State and Ferries was as high as airport so allow a little extra time.We felt very safe walking about, a few touts but not a major problem. Subway ticket was $2 which you used within two hours, or a Metrocard for $7 which gave unlimited bus and subway travel until 3am the next day. You can get to all 5 boroughs (Manhatten, Brooklyn, Bronx, Queens and Staten Island) with this. Also felt quite safe using public transport.Hope this helps and enjoy your stay.

Feb 20 2007 	Sweet Embassy	I had never stayed in one of the Embassy Suites chain before but after my experience at the Embassy Suites in New York I would not hesitate to be a repeat customer and recommend it to my friends. Having stayed in a number of hotels in New York, including the Waldorf, the Soho Grand, the Parker Meridien and others, I can honestly say that for the amount you are paying at the Embassy Suites you will not be able to find a comparable hotel in Manhattan. My room, which was a basic suite, had a living room with a minibar, mircrowave, tv etc and a large bright bedroom as well as a functional bathroom with granite counters. Considering the decidedly pokey rooms that I was used to in NYC I had a fantastic amount of space - in fact far larger than the tiny studio apartments of many friends who live in the city. In addition the room was kept beautifully clean, and the bed and bedding were very comfortable. There are a number of restaurants within the same building as the hotel, as well as a great many more within a short walk or cab ride. Perhaps my only reservation, which is entirely a matter of personal choice, is that the hotel's location is slightly too quiet if you are looking to stay in a lively neighbourhood. While there are all the amenities you could need nearby, the Battery Park/WTC area is, like most financial districts, not the richest or most exciting area culturally speaking. The area's upside is that it is very safe and a short cab ride to Tribeca, Soho and the Village and will be for many a far preferably option to the many overpriced slightly grubby hotels in those areas.All in all, having stayed in some of the best hotels in town like the Mandarin Oriental - the Embassy Suites acquits itself admirably. You won't get all the frills of a four or five star but the comfort and value for money are unparalleled.

Nov 5 2006	Fantastic Family Hotel!	We stayed here for 5 nights at the end of October with our 2 children and it was ideal. We had a 2 double bedded suite (tip - ask for a room on the 15th floor at the end of the corridor - nice and quiet). We found the room to be really clean and welcoming after a long journey from the UK; check-in was easy, and having called ahead to request an end of corridor room we had been obliged! The rooms don't have fridges (just mini-bars), however on requesting a fridge at check-in we had one delivered to our room within 30 minutes. In recent reviews I have read comments about the local building work, I have to say we heard absolutely nothing! Our room was along the side of the hotel which was away from the building works at the front and rear and I think that because we were on the top floor it helped. The free breakfast was just brilliant and set us up for the day; it was never particularly busy and had so much choice. With Children of 11 &amp; 13 the managers reception was a welcome rest at the end of a busy day touring NYC. You are given vouchers at check in which entitle you to a generous amount of free alcoholic drinks - the 'sodas' are free and vouchers weren't needed. They also provide free Nachos and Dips. After a sit down we would feel refreshed and ready to go out to eat! If you fancy a really good pizza in NYC - go to Lombardi's (google it), it was the best pizza ever and so reasonable. In terms of getting round NYC, we found the hotel really well placed, it was a 5 min walk to the nearest subway which got you into the heart of town in 10 mins max. Also the yellow cabs were always outside the hotel and I have to say they were really reasonable - just make sure they don't take you the long way round! If you fly to JFK, the yellow cabs line up outside arrivals and it costs only $45 flat fee to get to anywhere in Manhattan - well worth the fare. One final note, there are 6 free to use internet enabled PC's in the Reception area. We never had to wait to use them and the Children enjoyed being able to have 15 mins on them to chat to their friends at home!Anyway I could go on and on! Needless to say if we ever go back to NYC, we wouldn't stay anywhere other than Embassy Suites.

An apartment block is being built at an alarming rate and any view is being eroded on a daily basis. On the 'city view' side a new building is being built and it will not be long before that also affects any view but already the noise is beginning to build. I have always rated the Embassy chain throughout the whole of the US but would and could not recommend this hotel to anyone at present.

Oct 16 2006 	Perfect	I stayed in the Embassy Suites for a week at the end of September/beginning of October as part of a group of 4.We had a room with two double beds in the one bedroom and although at first we were a bit worried about lack of space it turned out no problem at all. Having the separate living area made all the difference to the suite, we had a view onto the Financial centre although you see the river to your right and the edge of the WTC site to the left. I take the point of not having refrigeration space in the room however there is a drinks and ice machine on every floor, and a small store beside reception selling snacks, drinks and souvenirs. Our room was on the top (15th) floor, which meant it was slightly quieter than other floors.There are 6 computers beside reception with free internet access, which were very handy for checking the football results back home! The breakfast was excellent; it was much busier at the weekend but nothing to horrendous. It was worth the wait, make sure you try the freshly made pancakes or omelettes at least once! It does last you most of the day, which makes it easier to fit in all the sightseeing. We never made it to the manager’s reception as we were never in the hotel during that time period, it did seem popular with other guests.The hotel is out of the very centre of town, but I enjoyed coming back to the peace and quiet of the area at night. The metro is a fantastic way of travelling around, the WTC stop on the blue line is the closest stop, you can obtain a Metro card at the station for 10 dollars which gets you 6 trips for the price of 5. Taxi's are always around, and are still a relatively in-expensive way of getting around.Check in and out was very easy, reception changed travellers cheques with no problems and booked tables at restaurants when we asked. The maid service was very efficient, and other members of staff were friendly to us. We asked the concierge to order us a taxi to the airport (Newark) and he got us one of the hotel cars to take us to the airport in comfort for a reasonable sixty dollars.I would thoroughly recommend going on the Circle Line 3 hour tour round the island, its the only way to realise how big Manhattan is! Top of the Rock is a much better experience than the empire state in my opinion, a less hectic atmosphere. Check out The Odeon in Tribeca and Pastis in Chelsea for good food. Definitely make time to visit St. Paul's Chapel (to the left of the WTC site as you're walking up from the hotel) which acted as a refuge for the rescue workers while clearing up the WTC site. I would definitely return to the Embassy Suites again and would recommend it to anybody.

Aug 17 2006 	Good Stay At Embassy Suites	Just returned from 7 nights with my wife and three kids (16, 13, 7). $349 on Friday and Saturday and $289 on other other nights having booked two months ago. It was on the 10th Floor overlooking the back street - American Express building and World Trade Center. This was quiet at night and no problem for us. The airconditioning was very good and adjustable. The bathroom and shower were also very good and towels changed, if desired, every day. The suite was very comfortable and we had no problems with noise. Warn kids about the mini-bar!The complimentary breakfast is excellent, especially with kids, and gives the day a good start. While we were down by 07:30 most days, there were no real problems with queues. On Saturday and Sunday there was some queuing at the counter serving omelettes and pan cakes. Breakfast consisted of cereals, coffee, teas, fruit drinks, different breads and bagels, fruit (melons, grapes, a[ples, bananas, oranges, Canadian bacon, sausages, hash browns, fried eggs, omelettes, pancakes, doughbuts, Danish pastries, muffins - in fact ,everything you could want!There are four screens with free internet access (+ USB ports and printing) in Reception. We had no time to use the 11 screen cinema and were never back in time for the manager's complimentary drinks reception at 17:30.Getting to the hotel from JFK:-We followed the directions to the SkyTrain in Arrivals and travelled to Howard Beach Station (note: you pay at Howard Beach station). Then we took the A Train to Chamber Street Subway station. You can buy a cheaper return SkyTrain+subway ticket from Howard Beach to Chamber Street Subway Station. At ChamberStreet we took the Vesy Street exit, emerging at the site of Ground Zero. The hotel is then a short two blocks walk. Note: returning to JFK, we accessed Chamber Street Subway via Church Street to take the A Train back to Howard Beach.For travelling to Manhattan:-Go to Church Street (two blocks away) for the nearest entrance to Chamber Street Subway (routes 1,2,3) for the West Side. We used City Hall/Brooklyn Bridge Subway (routes 4,5,6) for the East Side, three blocks away and easily walkable. Note: we also puchased weekly subway Metro Cards ($24 each) which proved very economical and saved a lot of time. The Subway was safe for us, even late at night, though we are used to travelling in cities.Family dining:-One block away behind the World Trade Center is PJ Rourkes where you can eat and drink overlooking the water with a view of the Statue of Liberty until the wee small hours. There is also a Pick-A- Bagel and a Mexican restaurant in the same block as the hotel. We took the very pleasant walk along the shoreline from the Hotel to Clinton Fort at Battery City Park (15minutes walk) and took the ferry trip to Liberty and Ellis island. We found the Heartland Brewery, beside the Empire State, at 350 Fifth Avenue at 34th Street , very good. The beer was also the best I found in Manhattan! We also had great pizzas at Lombardis in Little Italy (Subway 6 stop at Spring Street ) at 32 Spring St, between Mott and Mulberry Streets. For a real NYC experience, Katz's Delicatessan at 205 East Houston Street (corner of Ludlow Street) on the Lower East Side is a must-do for (used in the film Harry Met Sally... for that famous scene). The Metropolitan Art Museum also has an award winning restaurant in the basement and is also great for lunch.Shopping near the hotel:Century 21 is within 5 minutes walking diustance at the side of Ground Zero. J&amp; R is ten minutes walk away at Park Row, (across from City Hall Park and Ground Zero), where we found prices for iPOD's and digital cameras very competitive.Overall, this hotel is as good as the other reviewers say. It is very family friendly. The location is very good - you cannot be near everything in New York! The staff were very friendly and helpful. The concierge (Stan) was great with with directions and advice. Will we use Embassy Suites again? Yes, without hesitation. We are already planning our next trip!

Aug 5 2006 	A nice surprise away from Midtown	I visit NYC at least once a year and have never &quot;taken the plunge&quot; to stay in lower-priced Lower Manhattan. I always assumed it would be too inconvenient to Midtown attractions and, especially, theatre. Not the case. Other than the fact that we sweltered in 110 degree heat on the subway platform, we found transportation to Times Sq and theatres was an easy journey every time. Also, found it a lot less stressful to buy theatre tickets at TKTS booth at South Street Seaport rather than negotiating the mile-long line at the Times Sq location (temporarily relocated to the Marriott Marquis, by the way)I do not understand all the reviewer complaints about distance of this hotel from the subway. It's, at most, 3 blocks!! Altho, it may seem like it to new visitors to NYC, subway stops are NOT located on every corner in the city! It took us 10 min. max to get to and from the subway each trip. Didn't bother us at all (3 guys in their 50s and 60s). Given the outside air temps, it was a nice relief to get inside the hotel where the AC was pumping away VERY efficiently (in the lobby as well as our room).Enjoyed discovering Lower Manhattan. There is a LOT to do there in addition to the well-known jumping off spot for the Statue of Liberty. Battery Park City, surrounding the hotel, is a beautiful new residential area with a fabulous landscaped park all along the Hudson. Battery Park is an easy walk from the hotel. The Skyscraper Museum and the Museum of Jewish History are located along the way. The free Staten Island Ferry is a 20 minute walk, or 5 minute cab ride from the hotel.....as is South Street Seaport. Little Italy, Chinatown and the Eastside Tenement Museum are all 3 subway stops away. And, of course, the WTC site is practically across the street from the hotel, although one wonders how much of a plus that will be once full-blown construction of the new Freedom Tower gets underway right outside.Negatives: rooms are rather small by Embassy Suites standards. We asked for an upgraded room after our first night proved to be pretty cramped for 3 adults. Were given a Hudson River view room, but it was no larger. Lack of a refrigerator was an inconvenience.The complimentary breakfast in the lobby was a logistics nightmare. We tackled it only twice in our 6-day stay, because we never could figure out what &quot;early&quot; meant, i.e. the hotel's suggested time to avoid crowds. It was ALWAYS crowded and is set up very awkwardly for crowd control. We got much better food and service at the bagel shop that is located outside on the SE corner of the building. Also, there is a GREAT patisserie right next to Starbucks in the shopping mall across the street in the World Financial Center. Bottom line: will I return? I think so, given the outrageous rates being charged by Midtown hotels. We couldn't find anything under $500 this time of year (mid-July) in that area, and certainly appreciated the suite arrangement we had with 3 adults. $319 for a hotel room isn't cheap, but given the market and the caliber of accommodations, it was a great value.

Jul 13 2006	Nice stay overall but choose carefully....	We (3 adults, 2 kids) stayed at the Embassy Suites in late June 2006 for a couple nights. We had a good time, and I'm in general agreement with most of the other positive reviews here. Here are some additional considerations that may be helpful in planning your stay:Number in party: For hailing a taxi, 4 people is the maximum number that a taxi can legally take. After that, you're in limo-land at higher prices. We didn't know this - we figured we'd be able to take one of the van taxis, since they appeared to have room; but they are also limited to 4 passengers. We DID get one taxi driver to take our party of 5 back to the hotel from Times Square at the end of one very hot and exhausting day. He got a large tip. For the hotel, our party of 5 had no surcharges because we had 3 adults and 2 kids (kids= 18 years and below). However, I was told by the reservations office that any other configuration of 5 people would have resulted in an extra-bed surcharge. I never confirmed this, however.Location of room: The hotel rooms are only on 2 adjacent sides - one side facing the water to the west, and the other facing the World Financial Center to the south (with a view of the WTC site from a few rooms). We asked at check-in for a water view room, but were told that we could not be accommodated because we needed 2 beds in the bedroom -- only king bed suites face the water.Room size: Compared to other hotels in New York, the suite might be considered roomy -- but we felt that the suite wasn't exactly staggeringly spacious. Once the couch is unfolded into a bed, passage through the living room is impossible without moving furniture against the walls. The &quot;fridge&quot; is for mini-bar stuff only; bring a cooler for your own food.Room rate: I originally inquired in March about room rates, and was quoted $279/night as the best rate for the june stay. I should have reserved then (I could have cancelled it without penalty). One month later, the lowest public rate was $359. After much discussion with a helpful reservations clerk, I was finally able to get my company's negotiated rate at $315. Parking: If you drive in, parking is pretty outrageous anywhere you go (Also, the garage parking rate signs are intentionally confusing to read while cruising past, like &quot;$19.32 for the first 4 hours!&quot;. In addition, SUVs and sometimes minivans are surcharged $8-16 per day). The hotel charges $50/day for parking in their garage, and it's valet only. Since I didn't want to drive into the city in heavy traffic, we arrived on a Sunday. It turns out that this was a good day to also find parking, because I found free on-street parking in the East Village; in Greenwich Village; and on North End St (the street the hotel is on). You have to be willing to wait for a spot, and read the parking signs carefully - they absolutely ticket violators.Subway location: The closest subway stop (Chambers St) was 3 blocks away at a diagonal from the hotel. In the 95 degree heat, and with my 80 year old mother, walking this became a challenge a couple of times. One subtlety to subway passes: you can buy a FunPass ($7/day, unlimited rides); a single-ride pass ($2.50); or a discount pass (5 rides for price of 4 - $10). But the discount pass can only be used for 4 people going through a turnstile at the same time; the 5th person will need to purchase another pass.Ground Zero: St Paul's memorial was a moving experience. Most of the Ground Zero site is difficult to view; there are fences all around, and there is a lot of construction activity. One of the better viewing areas is from the arcade in the World Financial Center.Interesting stuff to do: In addition to the other activities people have discussed, we had a good time strolling the walking/biking path next to the water. It goes for miles in either direction. Also, South Street Seaport had a cadaver exhibit that was interesting - not for the squeamish. Our favorite typical tourist things were the Top of the Rock (said to be much better and much less waiting than the Empire State Building), NBC Studios, and a 45-min water taxi ride.Eating and drinking: We ate at a variety of places, and, surprisingly, didn't find the food to be that expensive. On the first day, we ate Sunday brunch at the Life Cafe in the East Village (near Tompkins Park) - highly recommended. (Portions of the movie Rent were filmed here, btw). The hotel complex includes an Applebees, a Chevy's (fairly good Mexican food chain), and a noodle shop. There is a small 24-hr grocery within walking distance of the hotel (turn right out the door, go north 3 blocks). The hotel breakfast is fine; we went early when it wasn't crowded. The afternoon manager's reception drinks were so-so, about what you'd expect for &quot;complimentary&quot;. Good time to unwind, tho.

May 23 2006	Gem on the Hudson	After reading such positive reviews on this website, I booked a 5-night stay at this hotel to serve as my home for my NYC explorations. Plenty of hotel staff to clear and clean tables. Going in either direction will bring much scenic treats - I brought my camera on 2 of the mornings to capture some spectacular images. There's plenty of other morning exercise-goers, so no worries about being alone.The nearest metro stop is about a 10-15 minute walk away (Chambers St. stop since the WTC stop was closed b/c the area is under construction at the time). It's a safe walk and well lit at night. The latest we returned home taking the metro was around 10-11pm and there were still plenty of other people walking the pathway from the metro to the hotel. Of course, cabs are an option and I did see plenty of them around but we never took one.Overall, would not hesitate to recommend this hotel to friends and family. A great value in NYC.

A good mixture of people in the morning, tourists, business, families &amp; couples. Easy going and informal.Staff in general were courteous and helpful. The Concierge was enthusiastic and helpful.Not one to knock a free drink but I think the description 'Managers reception' over glamourises this affair - don't think champagne and hors d'oeuvres but plastic 'glasses' and paper plates with nachos - however a nice touch and welcomed after a long day. Don't put your glad rags on for this.Choice of restaurants in the Hotel was adequate, my suggestion - your on Holiday - do as we did, explore and find one of the plentiful Irish Bars/Restaurants north of Hotel.To get to the main Tourist areas from this Hotel you need to get on the Subway or find yourself a Taxi at night. This will be costly after a week or so.Free internet access in the lobby a bonus. Overall a clean and spacious Hotel with adequate facilites, helpful staff and a great breakfast. Although perhaps a bit far from the action there is plenty to explore around the Hotel and it offers some great views from Battery Park. Beware, some building work directly in front of the Hotel but since no room seemed to face that direction it should not be a problem - call them if your worried.

Feb 25 2006	A Unique NYC Experience	Locating a place to stay in NYC for a family of 5 proved to be bigger challenge than I expected, after all, I worked in the city for many years and thought &quot;no problem&quot;. 95% of the hotels I called would require reserving 2 rooms due to fire codes. Embassy Suites could accommodate us in one space and sounded like the best choice, however I wasn't crazy about the financial district location. As it turned out, we all loved the hotel and found its location to be amazing. The Hotel staff was friendly, courteous and helpful. The rooms were spacious compared to most NYC hotels. Bathrooms were clean and roomy, however were short on bathroom tissue and towels at arrival. A phone call to the front desk fixed the situation in under 15 minutes. Beds were comfortable, except for the pullout couch, they definitely need to upgrade the mattresses here. 2 large TV's in each room helped with my 3 daughters (ages 17, 15, and 12) when needed. Breakfast and manager's cocktail reception, included in cost of room, are big money savers and are quite good. This hotel is located in a very quiet area which is nice after spending busy days and evenings in NYC (no fire engines honking in the middle of the nite). The Esplanade is a great place to enjoy the waterfront views and walk off a big meal. It's full of activity in the evening as many locals use it for roller blading, jogging, walking, etc. Definitely try a steaming bowl of Prince Edward Island mussels at Steamers on the Esplanade. Lots to see right in the area, Chinatown, Little Italy and Tribecca nearby for good eats. Battery Park within walking distance for Harbor tours, which I recommend doing the 45 min tour that takes you by the Statue of Liberty, bridges, Empire State, etc. rather than the Liberty Tour which has long lines and I believe they still don't let you climb up to the top of the Statue. I recommend you ask about that before booking. Broadway was about a $10 cab ride, we saw Phantom, it was awesome. We used Icon parking @ $35/day by Washington St to save on parking. RE: subways, we found taking a van-cab was only a couple of dollars more for us than travelling uptown by subway and a lot more enjoyable. From Central Park to Embassy, $15 including tip. In the middle of Aug, believe me, it was worth the extra 5 bucks for airconditioned cab and to be delivered directly to our awaiting hotel doorman... one of life's simple pleasures. Enjoy this hotel, it's a good deal!
