Jan 16 2006	Very nice experience - have a plan for breakfast	We planned our visit for the 3 days following Xmas - knowing this would be a busy time we booked ahead. We wanted someplace quiet, but within 15 minutes of the funspots. Using the Embassy Suites own webpage, we clicked the &quot;internet deals&quot; tab and was happy to commit to a rate of $189 a night. The only requirement was that there was a no-refund policy. This ALMOST bit us as the transit strike was not resolved until the 23rd. We parked the car in New Haven ($8 a day)and took Metro-north into the city. Booking in advance and using off-peak rates: 2 adults, a 13 years old and a 5 years travelled roumd trip of $89. DIRECTIONS: From Grand Central Station ($2 one trip pass or $7 all day pass) take the #4 train to Courtland Street (** there are three Courtland Street stations - the one on the # 1 train is closed **) the #4 train will drop you off at the church where the 9/11 rescuers rested and the place you will remember as the tall black iron fenceline with all the photos of the missing. It is all clean now and there is a nice memorial inside the church. When you exit the station head west (towards the back of the church) about 300 feet, and you will see the PATH train station (NJ bound) in front of you. If you turn left the white building is &quot;Century 21&quot; - reportedly the number 1 high-end clothing discount location in the world. Fortunately the hotel is to the right ... follow the fenceline of the PATH around the corner and it will lead you to a modern covered walkway which leads right to the hotel. As you take this walkway the footprint of the WTC will be on your left. There is an esclator and an elevator, so really no UP stairs. When you have crossed over West Street (4 lane roadway) you are at the end - follow the stairs ahead of you down. On your left is the American Express Building and the site of a nice shopping mall. The hotel is the brown building at your 2 o'clock position. You may notice the movie theather signs first. It was about a 5 minute walk with bags ... not a single complaint from either the 13 or 5 year old. Enter the glass doors and take the esclator up into the atrium of the hotel - as you walk towards the other side you will pass the evening reception / breakfast buffet room. The main hotel bank of elevators are to your right through the glass doors, BUT check in first downstairs. You can leave the others in the nice chairs or have them see the waterfall and continue across to the down esclator. The front desk will be to your right. While there notice the wall mounted flatscreen TV - to its right, is the 6 station (free) internet access. Immediately behind that is a little store and a hidden entrance to a great Asian Resturant with a nice take-out service. EXPERIENCE: We arrived around 11:30 am and intended to check our bags as we were headed to Broadway for a 2:30 show when the well groomed and attentive desk staff advised us that if we didn't mind staying on the second floor ( we had been booked on the 15th ) we could check in now. Room 232 was located on the main floor and allowed us to avoid using the elevators and placed us on the same floor as the drinks and food. Not a bad thing for a man and the world class NYC Fitness club was also accessable from the end of our hall. We were suprised at the amount of space ... nice 12' high ceilings and the feel of upscale appointment. The main room consisted of a sofa/couch, a cushioned chair and coffe table. The TV was nicely sized for the room and stored within a cabinet. To the left of the TV was a table and 3 chairs set aside for dining. There is also a wet bar with a food prep area and undercabinet microwave. The room lacks a refrigerator but I understand what a cleaning nightmare those must be for housekeeping. (I had heard a rumor that if you ask they will bring one up to your room.) The living area is separated from the bedroom by a cool, frosted glass wall and door. This room has a king sized bed. It displayed (5) full down-pillows and 1 body pillow which was 4 feet long. The mattress was one of the most comfortable we have enjoyed anywhere in the world. The room has a great view of the Hudson River and the New Jersey Skyline. Our 5 year old fell asleep on the nice sitting area in front of the windows later that night. The room came with one terry-cloth robe and again a nice sized TV in a multi-funtion cherry cabinet. The bathroom was very clean, it had Bath &amp; Beautyworks supplies and the offer if any items were left at home (razor / shaving cream / toothbrush / toothpaste / comb ...) that they would provide free of charge at the desk. You can't beat that. The room is equipped with the traditionals such as coffee maker and hairdryer ... the bathroom night light was welcomed as I forgot to bring ours. We never heard our neighbors, no hall noise and not a sound from the street, so we were very happy with the hotel construction design. BUFFET PLAN OF ATTACK: It was a very busy time and the hotel was at full occupany, even with the posted times for stress-free buffet eating it was alittle crazy. If you find it busy when you go, a simple 3-prong attack works best. Have someone secure a table. The &quot;eggs made to order&quot; line only provides eggs, nothing else ... so one person goes there with multiple orders. The buffet line has multiple stations, overload a plate or two with stuff your doctor probably doesn't need to know about - bacon, sausage and potatos and have your own buffett at the table. After the food portion of the line, skipping the line is allowed - return for the juice/drinks and silverware. There is a seperate area at the end of the serving are for fruits, breads, bagels, pancakes, cereals ... This is the bargin of the century - a breakfast of this quantity &amp; quality, anywhere else in New York would easily be $25 a person. Same goes for the mangers reception every night, quality drinks and snacks, nice room and fun music ... a chance to meet other people for around America or the world ... for the price of a tip. We found it easy TO GET AROUND from the hotel. While the metropass allows bus use and the M20 does stop nest to the hotel and go to Times Square - it was a long wait but a GREAT ride through the neat neighboorhoods along the way ... it was night and christmas - more than once we commented on how fun it would be to have alittle place here. The bus was not a time effective way to travel though. From the hotel to TIMES SQUARE you can either take a $2 taxi to the #1 train @ Chambers Street (walkable - but lots of traffic and very dark at night) or . HEARLD SQUARE/ROCKERFELLER CENTER - Walk to the back of the church (across from the PATH) and take the #R,N,Q or W train to Herald Square and transfer to the # B,D, F and V. To get to 59TH STREET area or up the line to YANKEE STADIUM walk to the church and take the #4 train (Courtland Street). If you want to get to COLUMBUS CIRCLE, PORT AUTHORITY BUS TERMINAL or PENN STATION walk to the PATH station itself and follow the signs to the # A,C or E train. CENTRAL PARK is easily accessed this way to also. Including Columbus Square the next 6 stops exit into the park and the upscale Central Park West. Back at the hotel you will find a very safe &amp; clean walking path along the river and a super CHILDREN's play area, both are located only 300' out the door by the front desk esclator. We were not willing to spend half a day or more to view the Statute of Liberty and a local let us in on the best HIDDEN JEWEL in NYC. We took a $5 taxi which took us thru the upscale Battery Park City past the unbelieveable line of people standing in line for the tour (blocks long) and to the Staten Island Ferry Terminal. This ultra-modern building has a nice store and we quickly boarded the FREE ferry to the island - wonderful views of the Brooklyn and Verrazano Bridge's, water traffic in the harbor and you pass both Ellis Island and the Statute. The 20 minute ride was relaxing with plenty of photo op's ... and it was big fun for our 5 year old. Upon our arrivial we simly exited the ferry and got back in line for the FREE return trip. We sat next to a tour group and learned alot from their guide. All told it was an hour round-trip. We noted while in Staten Island the presence of the New York Yankee minor league park which faces the skyline - will have to return for a nightgame, the views must be stunning. We have nothing but positive things to say about the Embassy Suites - NYC, nice, clean and spacious room, great price (still not sure why we got such a low price, reasonable access to transportation and a nice quiet spot in NYC. WE WILL BE BACK ... we also had a nice experience at another ES in Deerfield Beach, FL (next to Boca Raton) - right on the beach, great pool, billion dollar views, all beach toys, floats ... provided at no charge ... twice daily complimentary chilled orange slices delivered pool and beach side. Similar breakfast buffet and happy hour ... the internet rate there was only $159. Enjoy

In summary, this is a fab place to stay. I was a little concerned about staying in Lower Manhattan but needn't have been. I would definately return in the future.	
Dec 11 2005	Extremely comfortable but beware of spotty cell phone service	This was our second stay at this hotel, both times in December. Ironing board, two desks, lots of lamps, upgraded bedding and extra pillows, very soft and large towels. It's not luxurious in the fittings and fixtures, but I'd rather sacrifice a marble bathroom for plenty of space. But the best part is the picture window and fabulous views of the Hudson and New Jersey. We have paid this much and more at midtown hotels and not even gotten a glimpse of the sky to see what the weather is. I'm sick of doing that, which is why we now go downtown. I like the location as well. I can walk to Tribeca for great shopping and restaurants and subway uptown. And it's only a 6-minute walk to Century 21, the BEST discount department store I've ever seen. (Get a good night's sleep and go early.)Back to the room: the little sign on the desk said there was wireless internet, but we didn't have any signal, so we connected with the cord. A few minutes after we arrived in our room, the fellow who checked us in actually called us to see if our room was okay and if we had any questions - I was SHOCKED. We've stayed at many 4-5 star hotels in midtown and this has never happened before. I'm a little on the high-maintenance side, and everyone, without exception, was friendly and helpful. I commandeered a non-English-speaking kitchen worker who gladly filled my styrofoam cup with with milk for my next morning's tea.We stayed three weeknights and left on a Friday. The hotel was full the whole time we were there, but Friday at checkout was the first time it appeared crowded - lines to check in, and I wasn't crazy about the piles of luggage I saw by the bell stand and front door, not completely unattended but not totally secure, either. Tips: request the view you want, either river or city, and a high floor for a better view. Bad news: our cell phones (Sprint and T-Mobile) did not get consistent reception in the living room. We often had to stand by the window in the bedroom to get reception, which means you can't make a call while sitting at the large desk in the living room.Hope this helps - it's so hard to know what other people feel is good value. Nov 11 2005	New York's Embassy Sweet	I've been in the hotel business for several years now. I must say that the Embassy Suites, New York City, ranks right up there as one of the best for the money that I've ever seen. Here's a few reasons why.TROY, CONCIERGE. Bent over backwards on the phone to make sure our upcoming visit would be special. Meet him and you'll understand.SERVICE. Ever wonder what happened to that once-taken-for-granted thing called 'service?' Well it's alive and well at the ESNYC. I arrived a little grumpy after spending almost 3 hours in a shuttle from LGA. The front desk didn't miss a beat-they immediately stressed the fact that I had finally made it to the hotel, and that they were glad my wife and I had decided to stay there. The housekeeping staff is quite respectfull of your wishes, and do a great job. Everywhere I went in the hotel, someone was cleaning something. Also, whenever we'd leave/enter the hotel, we were always told to enjoy our day, or were welcomed back.LOCATION. This seems to be the only 'problem' to some staying at the ESNYC. Actually, there's lots to do downtown. There's a great promenade just below the hotel that leads all the way down to Battery Park, where you can ferry over to Ellis Island, Staten Island (free-do it for the Manhattan photo ops on the way back!). From Battery Park, just walk up Broadway, and you'll pass by Ground Zero (just two blocks from ESNYC), and the rest of the financial district. Don't forget the Brooklyn Bridge which starts at Park Row.In the other direction, walk out of the hotel and turn right. Go north on the West Side Highway a few blocks, then turn right on Chambers (use the footbridge). Now you're in Tribeca, an up to now passed over neighborhood for tourists. Robert DiNiro lives here somewhere, and his restaurant group has two offerings: Nobu, and Next Door Nobu (easier of the two to get a table). Walk around the Hudson Street area. It's very neighborhoody and not overrun with tourists. Go right on Canal St. On one side is Chinatown, on the other, Little Italy (Mulberry St.). Don't forget a walk through SOHO, maybe get a drink at Broome Street Bar.Keep walking north a few blocks, and before you know it you're right up on NYU/Waverly Place and Washington Square (people watching central!).Too complicated? Just walk up Broadway from Battery Park. You'll see plenty.So it's the gritty city you want to see? I've got two words for you: Delancy Street.See? There's a lot downtown. The cool thing about walking in New York, is the amount of ground you'll cover without even realizing it. On the map things look farther than they are when you're on the sidewalk taking in this great city. One day, I walked from the ESNYC all the way to Central Park South, taking in the city the whole way.Drawbacks? Not many. Taxis can get expensive if you're darting around the city. Don't be afraid of the subway and the busses, especially in the daytime. They both are cheap as hell and fast. For example, a taxi ride to the Theatre District/Times Square will run you about $12. The subway costs $2, no matter where you're going. Just a thought. I know some people can't muster the bravery they think they'll need.CLEANLINESS. The first thing my wife does when we check into a hotel (we travel a lot), is check the bathroom and sheets. Believe me, if she says it's clean, it's beyond clean! ESNYC passed with flying colors.THE ROOMS. These are all suites, which make them the largest rooms available at this price in the city. A lot of $1800 a month apartments in New York are smaller than these rooms!If you absolutely have to be in Midtown, perhaps you should look at another property. If you want a downtown experience at a hotel with great harbor and city views, the ESNYC is a great choice. It all comes together here. I will be back.Kudos, GM Mark Thomson!Questions? Email me. Also, see my review of the Hotel Pulitzer, Amsterdam, if you're heading that way!	
Nov 8 2005	Fantastic - would definitely stay here again	My wife booked us a long weekend in New York for my 40th birthday. It was our first time in New York and having read the reviews of where we were originally going to stay (which was somewhere off Broadway around 103rd Street) we asked the company we'd booked through to change the hotel. This was the option out of the two we were given that we chose - and I'm glad we did!Here are our opinions:The roomsAll rooms are off the hotel atrium which gives a very light and airy feel – no long corridors making it feel closed in. We had a double-bedded suite which was very clean and pleasant. Basically it consisted of a sitting room with sofa, table &amp; chairs and television, bathroom with shower and very small bath and the bedroom with plenty of storage space and television. Our room looked out onto the World Financial Center – and if we craned our necks we could actually see the Hudson River, so although we didn’t have a river view as such, the outlook was still pretty good. There wasn’t a great deal of traffic about so the room was very quiet, there were some road works going on but even these didn’t disturb us.The room was cleaned and bed made every day, new towels in the bathroom.Tea and coffee making are provided – however if we wanted tea we had to use the coffee maker to make it! The mini-bar is also very well stocked, however I can’t comment on how the stocking levels were maintained as we didn’t use it. Also just below the mini-bar is a safe – which certainly came in very handy.LocationSome reviewers have said they didn't like the location, that the wasn't a subway nearby and it was a bit quiet on the streets on an evening. Okay so there isn't a subway right on the doorstep - but a pleasant 10-minute or so walk along the riverside (and yes it is right by the river - the only thing between it and the river path are a two lane road and the Irish Hunger Memorial) and you arrive at Battery Park, from where you can pick up the subway from Bowling Green station or a short walk up Broadway to Wall Street station.Chambers Street subway station is within easy walking distance also – but we preferred the walk south along the river.We didn’t use the buses, but there are plenty that run and stop at the back of the hotel and there are plenty of cabs (and limousines during the week) hanging around the hotel awaiting customers.The view across the river from the front of the hotel is fantastic and it is peaceful. The hotel is next door to the World Financial Center, the World Trade Center site is only a stone’s throw away, Battery Park is only a very short distance away from where you can catch numerous ferries. There were some nice boats moored at North Cove – including Ellen MacArthur’s B&amp;Q trimaran! Close by there are several museums namely the Museum of Jewish Heritage, the Skyscraper Museum and the Museum of the American Indian. We also found it an easy walk to the Seaport Historic District and the Brooklyn Bridge.We flew into JFK airport and caught a shuttle bus – and because the hotel isn’t slap bang in the centre of town we were the last to be dropped off. On a rainy Friday night it took 2 hours from leaving JFK to being dropped off at the hotel.People expect different things from hotels and their locations – you don’t go to New York and expect it to be peaceful – but to be honest after a day out in the hustle and bustle it was nice to come back here and be able to relax in peaceful surroundings.The StaffWe can’t fault the staff one bit – they were very helpful, courteous and knowledgeable, they greeted you with a smile and were always well turned out. There are plenty of reception staff so you’re not kept waiting to check in. There is a concierge who will help with advising on and booking tickets for excursions as well as helping with directions and giving advice on how to get around the island. The bellhops and door staff were also cheery, polite and very helpful.The complimentary breakfast and Manager’s receptionTo have breakfast as part of the deal proved to be a real bonus! There was plenty of choice ranging from bacon, sausages, cooked potatoes, eggs cooked any way you wanted them, fresh fruit, cereal, bagels, bread, toast, fruit juice, coffee, tea – in fact just about everything you could ever want for breakfast. Indeed it was that good we managed to fill up so that we didn’t need to stop for lunch while we were out and about. It can get a bit crowded, but we went down just after 8am and that seemed to be a good time as there was hardly any queuing.The manager’s free drinks reception is also part of the deal and again this is a real bonus. Basically from 5:30pm to 7:30pm the hotel bar is open, serving free beer, wine, spirits, cocktails – they even throw in snacks such as popcorn and chips (crisps). Obviously it is very popular but having said that we had no problems finding a seat nor did we have any problems getting served – no more than a couple of minutes wait. Remember though this bar is in America – so although the drinks are free you’ll still need your dollar bills for tips! Something also to bear in mind once the Manager’s reception is finished the bar closes – which means you’ll need to visit one of the other establishments within the hotel complex or head off into town if you want to continue drinking.FacilitiesThe hotel appears to have a restaurant of it own call ed the Unity but this was closed while we were there. However there are several restaurants as part of the hotel complex – there is Chevy’s Fresh Mex, which serves, as you’d expect, Mexican food. We sampled it and it was pretty good – and very reasonable. This is actually inside the hotel, right next to the hotel bar. Outside there is Applebees Neighborhood Bar &amp; Grill – which we also sampled. We didn’t rate this quite as highly as Chevy’s and the price wasn’t as reasonable either. Other restaurants (that we didn’t sample) include Pac Rim – which serves sushi, Lili’s Noodle Shop – which served Chinese and Pick-a-Bagel which serves bagels, sandwiches, etc.If you’re that way inclined the room service menu was pretty extensive too!The complex also boasts an 11 screen cinema and as a guest you also get free use of the fitness facilities – but as we were only there for three nights we didn’t use either of these.In summary if you want a nice quiet hotel with decent facilities and don’t mind being out of the centre of town then I’d recommend the Embassy Suites every time.	
Nov 6 2005	for a family of 4 this is a great hotel	After arriving on Saturday late at night we checked in to the hotel. We had a couple of teething problems with the booking but this was sorted out very well with the Front Desk.We found that having the big breakfast(part of the price) set us up for the whole day and the only time we felt a little hungry was late afternoon, but we did not need a big meal at all. Oct 20 2005	Good value and very family friendly!	Very nice and new hotel. Friendly service. Oct 12 2005	Location is Great!	This is why garage sales work so well. What is one man's trash is another's treasure.:)We found the location of the Embassy Suites perfect for our needs. We got a 7-day Metro card. The M22 bus stops right outside the back door and whisks you to the Chambers Street subway stop, from which you can get anywhere. The M20 is across the street and takes you to the ferry stop for Statue of Liberty and Ellis Island tours. It also goes down 7th Avenue which is a quick way back to the hotel from Greenwich Village. The Connection bus is FREE and takes you everywhere &quot;downtown&quot;; including the Seaport area. We loved the fact that after being &quot;shoulder to shoulder&quot; with people all day sightseeing we could return to this locale with an open view of the horizon and the Hudson River. It was quiet enough to sleep with the windows open at night like we do at home. (We find that when we can have natural air at night we awake more rested.) We never even considered taking a taxi. With the Metro card such a good deal and public transportation so convenient it seemed silly to waste the money. We have used public transportation in many locations and found NYC to be complex but also complete. I doubt there is anywhere you need to get that can't be done via the buses and subway. For the record, the buses are immaculate and appear to be almost brand-new. Way cleaner than the subway, and maybe even safer since the driver is right there with you.The rest of the hotel is exactly as written by others. The service was outstanding, the room is spacious by normal standards albeit a bit smaller than some Embassy Suites we have stayed at. Breakfast and evening cocktails were excellent and represent a genuine value. About the fridge. The morning after we arrived I simply stopped by the front desk and asked to have either have the Honors Bar stuff removed or a different fridge delivered. When we got back from our day a new mini-fridge had been delivered and turned on so it was cold and ready.No additional charge. The guest laundry was useful even though there is only one washer and one dryer, found on Floor 9. (I was told by hotel staff that this is the ONLY smoking floor by the way. This means that the entire hotel was remarkably free of secondhand smoke which is another huge asset in our minds.)With all due respect, I disagree that the location should make you wary. We all travel with different needs and parameters for what makes a good hotel. For us this was a good choice and we would stay there again.	
Oct 9 2005	Location location location - Beware!	This was my 6th trip to NYC. In the past we have stayed at the Doubletree and the Marriott in Times Square, The Carlton, W, and this week we stayed at Embassy Suites. The pros: largest accomodations we've had, better than average free breakfast, staff was very accomodating and courteous, walls are soundproof, beds were comfortable, kids loved free internet in lobby, good choice of on site restaurants to choose from, movie theatre on premises (but who comes to NYC to go to the movies!). Cons: The closest subway station is Cortland (3 blocks) but it is closed for another year. The closest subway stations otherwise are Rector or by City Hall. It is a good 15 minute walk IF you are physically able and are NOT carrying large shopping bags or have small children. I can imagine the walk would be miserable in the cold winter! The 15 minutes walk feels like 3 miles when you have spent the entire day walking or when it's raining! Although I personally did not have any negative encounters, walking the distance after dark can be a little scary. There were not many other pedestrians out after 9:00 p.m. Plan on using taxis. We were told we were given a room with a refrigerator but the only refrigerator was the one with the sundries for a fee already stocked. Overall, the accomodations rated a B+, but due to the inconvenient location I would not recommend it until Cortland subway station opens or you are okay with taking taxis ($) frequently.

The hotel is about three blocks from the Chambers subway stop and you pass through a pedestrian walkway over the WTC site on your way to Chambers. There is a gorgeous view of the Hudson River on one side of the hotel, and across the street there is a lovely playground beside the river, with a view of the Statue of Liberty. I would definitely stay here again if I brough my kids to NYC- definitely more to my taste than hotels in the Times Square area.

Our family of six included my husband and I and 4 daughters 15, 17, 18 and 21. We never felt cramped in the room. The great free breakfast saved us a lot of money and time. Some of us got in the made to order omelot, oat meal, and pancake line and others went to the hot buffet line which had scrambled eggs, bacon, sausage, yogurt, grapes, bagels, juice, milk and more. By the time the girls finished breakfast they were actually awake and would then go back up to the room and quickly get ready for the day.My oldest daughter said her favorite thing in New York City was the hotel and the hotel breakfast!The area of the hotel is very nice and quiet and peaceful. There are many things to see in the area and we bought the one day subway and bus passes for $7 on Sat and Sunday and were able to get to midtown and upper Manhattan and back fairly easily. The M20 Bus is great and the bus stops right across the street from the hotel, around the corner from the front door. We also took the free connection bus to the South Street Seaport and Battery Park. The stop is also across from the Hotel near the M20 stop. We got the Bus schedule for all busses at the information desk of Grand Central terminal. It shows all the bus routes on a map and then gives when the bus runs and how often for different times of day AM, afternoon, evening, night. The actual times and routes are also posted on the posts with the bus stop signs. some buses go uptown on one street and downtown (lower manhattan) on another. We never really rode buses before but got the hang of it after awhile. We only took a taxi once and we actually needed two for the six of us. We were going to see All Shook Up on Broadway and were running too late to take a bus or subway. It was about $15 per taxi including tip from the hotel to Broadway and 46th St. The girls had never been in a taxi before and thought it was cool zipping around in and out of the traffic. The show was lively and we all liked it, especially the girls. We sat in the upper balcony, the $19.55 seats and the view was fine Everyone in the balcony kind of leans forward to get a good view. The price was right and we had fun walking around in the crowds on Times Square under the bright lights after the show. We took the M20 bus back to the hotel after the show.We also took the subway several times, only the subway station is farther from the hotel and we felt better walking across the street to the hotel from the bus stop in the dark rather than several blocks from the subway station. Also the subway trains were air conditioned but the stations where you wait were not and were often very hot! We got the subway map from the front desk at Embassy suites. We also got a nice map of all of Manhattan (with large print you could actually read) at the front desk. There was a pad of them on the counter and you could just tear one off and take it. We drove over to Brooklyn Friady night and my husband drove around differnt areas of Manhattan on Sun and Monday. He ended up with a $35.00 parking ticket on Sunday. He also got honked at a lot and almost hit a few times. I would recommend other modes of transportation! He somehow found a place to park free on the street two of our nights and put the car in a parking garage nearby one night for about $35.00We had a city view out our window but when we walked from our room to the elevator we had an awesome view of the water and a small park next to the hotel. I don't think you need to pay extra for a view. We were mainly in our room to sleep and dress so we rarely even opened our curtains.We felt pretty safe just about everywhere we went in New York City. We walked quite a bit. It is easier to get a feel for the neighborhoods by walking.

Two blocks away is the subway and the Century 21, plus more shops and restaurants.The biggest complaint I had was that the internet service was VERY shaky and kept kicking me off every few minutes. There's a $10 daily charge for highspeed wireless that's ordered through a separate provider, not through Embassy Suites. Unless they get their act together, skip it.This is not a Times Square location and things close down fairly early in the Financial District. So if you want to party all night, be prepared to take a taxi. And there are no little grocers on every block like you see in other districts.But, all in all, a very nice hotel, super terrific amenities and a decent location for a low price. All of the hotel staff we had contact with were very helpful and courtious and there is a constant flow of taxis outside. We generally used the bus system which runs from alongside the hotel, takes between 30 and 60 mins to get to the heart of the city depending on time of day. The 7 day unlimited metrocard gives unlimited use of subway and buses (24 dollars). After a long day uptown it was GREAT to get back and make use of the 2 hours complimentry drinks session, everything is free except for the voluntary 1 dollar tip, its well worth it and is highly recommended. Drinks are served in plastic containers but hey....its free, get over it! The rooms are very well appointed massive kingsize bed, two TV's, microwave, minibar (reasonably priced) and loads of space. If i HAD to pick a down point, and its a minor one really, the elevators can sometimes take a while arriving at peak times but i guess thats the same the world over. If i was to go back to NYC i WOULD DEFINATELY use this hotel again. I am a critical person so this statement is not given lightly.

Mar 11 2005	A Hotel I Will Come Back To	My husband and I went to NYC to visit my family in February 2005; and we wanted a hotel near my folks. We bought 4 nights through Hotwire for $169/night. At the time, that was about a $50 savings from all the travel web sites I’ve been to. (No, Hotwire does not show you the name of the hotel before you purchase; but we surmised from the description that it was Embassy Suites.) We did not drive to NYC (nor do you need to have a car in NYC); and therefore, do not know what the parking situation is like. However, I do recall seeing a few parking lots near the hotel. The hotel is right across the street from the World Financial Center and very close to the WTC site. The subway, which takes you to wherever you want to go in NYC (even JFK airport), is about 4 blocks away (Chambers Street Station). A few TripAdvisor writers have complained about the walk to the subway station, which really isn't that far. Listen, you are in a city, be prepared to walk to many of the places you want to go see. NYC has a fantastic public transportation system that New Yorkers themselves use everyday. They can take you close to, if not right to, the places you want to go. However, you still must be prepared to walk a bit in NYC. You can find subway and bus maps and information on the web site: -----.Anyway, back to the hotel. The front desk staff was extremely friendly, as was most of the staff at the hotel. We were never treated differently because of purchasing through Hotwire. In fact, without asking, we were upgraded to a wonderful suite overlooking the Hudson River.The suite is roomy. By NYC standards, it’s a good size. You definitely have room to stretch out. All the rooms were very clean. Décor is modern, with blond wood being the prominent theme. The bathroom is standard, with no surprises. Water pressure and hot water were never a problem when we were staying there. Bath and Body Works toiletries were a very nice touch. Housekeeping did a wonderful job. Our maid always made sure we had all the toiletries. The complimentary buffet breakfast was convenient with the selection being decent, although not very tasty. The hotel shares the building with a Regal Cinema, DSW Shoe Warehouse, and a few other restaurants, which may be convenient to some. We did contemplate a movie one night but decided against it because we were too tired.A few TripAdvisor writers have mentioned the walls being thin. I really did not hear much except when our neighbor flushed the toilet. My husband did hear our neighbor singing in the shower one day. But overall, we had a quiet room, with a great view, to come back to everyday. We had a very pleasant hotel experience; and I will try to get this hotel whenever we come back to NYC.

Aug 31 2004	Hard to imagine anything better!!!	Our family of five just returned from a 4 night stay at the Embassy Suites in Lower Manhattan, and we cannot imagine anything better in NYC. There are a lot of different locations to stay in New York, so you have to choose the best options for what you are looking for. The Embassy is down near Battery Park in a quieter section of the city...perfect for us. Late night strolls by the river for great views of Jersey City and the Statue of Liberty, easy walks to the subway, short stroll to the Ground Zero site (very emotional), great place to jog in the morning by the river, and a convenient, free bus shuttle service that takes you to such lower Manhattan sites as the ferry station, Seaport Village, and Wall Street. However the walks to all of these are short, and it's really not even that long of walk to Little Italy or Tribeca.As for the hotel itself, the room was plenty big for all five of us....kids in one room, us in the other. The breakfast was as good as it gets...fresh omelettes, pancakes, bacon, sausage, cereal, juices, fruit, etc. There is an Applebees and Chevys on site, as well as a great bagel/deli shop that we used a few times, especially at night for a late night treat. There is even a movie theatre that our kids used once. The concierge was extremley helpful, as were the bellmen and other employees. In fact, the kids said this was the best hotel they've ever stayed in!If you want the bright lights and the glamor, maybe the Times Square, Broadway, Rockefeller Center areas would be better for you, but once you realize how easy the subway system is, this area can't be beat. One train to Central Park (don't miss the Imagine memorial for John Lennon), one train to Yankee Stadium, one train to Greenwich, etc. Go and experience all of NY during the day and night, but come back to this peaceful, safe area and hotel for your stay. You will not be disappointed!

Mar 22 2004	Great place to stay for a weekend visit	My family (3) stayed at this hotel between 3/19 and 3/21. Mar 22 2004	Great Hotel	We just got back from our weekend in NY and we were quite pleased with the hotel. Our room was on the 15th (top) floor with a view of Ground Zero. The beds are a bit on the soft side but comfortable. The worst part about the room was the shower...terrible water pressure and the walls are a bit thin. We loved the fact that the hotel was quiet with respect to outside noise. We never heard traffic below. The complimentary full breakfast and drinks in the afternoon were phenomenal. We parked in the lot next door which charges 21.95/day but they will give a discount to hotel guests. Don't pay the $45 to park at the hotel. The lot is manned 24 hours/day and the attendants provided excellent service. The hotel is within walking distance to the ferries for Liberty and Ellis Islands and of course to Ground Zero, but you will need to take a cab or subway to Midtown, Chinatown or elsewhere. We've also stayed at the Marriott in Brooklyn but for the price you can't beat this hotel. Its roominess and amenities far exceed any of the other hotels. I wouldn't dream of staying anywhere else in NY now.	
Feb 23 2004	Comfortable base in NYC	We stayed on a family break here in Feb 04 - our first visit to NY. The hotel itself was very comfortable and the inclusive breakfasts were first class. Good reasonable dining facilities right next door. Spacious rooms - but in hindsight we would have been better with a double bedded room rather than the huge single bed; but the sofa bed meant that four of us fitted in without any problem. The location of the hotel has its good and bad points. Right on the river for superb views and fairly quiet in the evening - but it's a good five minute walk across a busy thoroughfare to the nearest subway. The staff were very helpful and friendly - but for some reason for one day that we were there we had no housekeeping or cleaning services. But all in all I would recommend the hotel and would be more than happy to go back there again.

Sep 17 2003	Great place to stay	Really enjoyed our stay and the Embassy Suites. The FREE breakfast is certainly not your average free breakfast - lots and lots of chow, omelets, eggs to order, pancakes, fruit, pastry, somebody rated the coffee weak - not during the 5 days we stayed. Bus up town and past the subway is just around the corner. If you are going to use the bus and subway, spring for the $14 dollar a day pass and despite what the brochures tell you you can only transfer from subway to the bus and NOT vice versa for no charge - except if you are using the Day Pass - it really makes it easy and in the long run cheaper. The concierge staff were wonderful - they really have a lot of knowledge and are quick to find the answer if they don't. Staff was great - always friendly and when I found the stopper in the tub did not function it was fixed right away. The threaters in the building is great. The FREE drinks in the evening is wonderful - while they limit the concoctions to the simpler drinks (Dude Lebowski would be unhappy without his White Russians) and they don't serve Guinness except at the downstairs bar which isn't free. The water front is great for walking and you can see Ellis Island and the Statue of liberty from the front windows. If you want to rent a bike, take your own lock - they won't give you one at the bike rental places as they then assume the liability if they get stolen. It is pretty easy to learn the subway system (I was surprised) though we had to double back once when we didn't realize the train we were on skipped a number of intermediate stops. New York was wonderful - the people were nice as they could be (they are going to lose their reputation if they keep this up for long - or is their chutzpah just urban legend.) Stay at the Embassy Suites - very nice indeed.

Aug 24 2003	Goin to NYC ? Trust me stay here!!!	Having visited NYC twice before ( 1st = marriage proposal, 2nd = U2 at Madison Square Gardens) I had already experienced much of the sublime along with some of the ridiculous that make this filmscape city so highly regarded and loved. On the hotel front, 'value' normally means paying horrendous rates to sleep in bog standard room and be surrounded by uptight business people or the upper tax bracket mob who'd complain if the front desk staff didn't greet them every day with a sickly inane grin. I'd stayed in tourist trap central (42nd street) and I'd stayed in 'boutique style' dump so needed to find some wracky style value for money! Well look no further people, this is it. Situated on the quiet banks of the Hudson River (next to the more laid back Financial District) and within touching distance of the bus,taxi,subway,water taxi systems this has to be a jewel in the embassy suites crown! You'll leave your roomy pristine suite of a morning to be greeted with sunshine pouring into the huge lobby atrium (14 odd floors high) and a panoramic view of the Hudson, sit yourself at a table and load yourself up for the day with FREE buffet brekkie with cooked to order omelettes. Other than starving yourself, this will save you alot of dosh. After a hard day covering this vast metropolis you will return to the same bar to be served FREE beer and cocktails by friendly waitresses from 5.30pm- 7.30pm! Remember, you are in Manhattan not Heaven ! Got kids in tow ? No problem, they'll have ample restaurants to choose for a burger &amp; fries followed by a choice of movies on the multi-screen cinema which are all part of this stunning hotel complex so they won't even have to leave the building ! On a more sombre note, it is obviously worth mentioning that only 1 block across the road, is the gaping chasm of Ground Zero. Hopefully, this should not be a deterrant to staying, but a lasting memory of incomparable bravery in a city that experienced unbelievable horror and continues, as does this hotel, to rise up through the ashes !
